<div id="review_1693965589" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1693965589" />
    <a title="Andy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5841469-andy"><img alt="Andy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597282744p2/5841469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1693965589?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/5841469-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5841469-andy?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5841469-andy?shelf=trash">trash</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1693965589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1371323237921382798">Mermaids that Eat People & are Kind of Bitchy<br/>Wake (Watersong #1)<br/>Rating: 1.5/5<br/><br/>Summary: When three beautiful girls come to the small town of Capri, Gemma and her sister are suspicious. The girls are eerily beautiful and are completely pretentious. They don’t speak to anyone, but they want to speak to Gemma. Gemma is a swimmer and she goes out for nightly swims in the bay by her house. One night, the girls entrance her to join them and her life is never the same.<br/><br/>This book had a lot of potential. It</span>
  <span id="freeText1371323237921382798" style="display:none">Mermaids that Eat People &amp; are Kind of Bitchy<br />Wake (Watersong #1)<br />Rating: 1.5/5<br /><br />Summary: When three beautiful girls come to the small town of Capri, Gemma and her sister are suspicious. The girls are eerily beautiful and are completely pretentious. They don’t speak to anyone, but they want to speak to Gemma. Gemma is a swimmer and she goes out for nightly swims in the bay by her house. One night, the girls entrance her to join them and her life is never the same.<br /><br />This book had a lot of potential. It wasn’t completely horrible, but it could have been a lot better. There didn’t seem to be much plot, nothing really happened until like halfway through besides talking and thinking. Her dad forgot her lunch a lot. This book is also strangely narrated. Its main narrators are Gemma and Harper, but we get the thoughts of Alex and a couple others mixed in. <br /><br />The romance was boring for me. Alex &amp; Gemma’s relationship had the potential to be one of those cutesy girl/boy next door relationships but it was just awkward. I could tell they liked each other, but I didn’t feel invested in their relationship at all. I was indifferent at best. Now Harper &amp; Daniel’s relationship had some real potential to be steamy and an adrenaline rush of falling head over heels. It was not. Every time they were alone together I was waiting for the sparks to fly off the page and to be consumed by romance and feels. I was thoroughly disappointed. Almost every time Harper makes a wrong move and the moment just failed miserably. It was really frustrating because I thought they had great chemistry.<br /><br />Another problem was that I really didn’t get attached to the characters. I didn’t really like Harper all that much, she was too controlling, bossy and almost always berating Gemma. She really needed to stop. Gemma was better but when it came to making the decision about her life as a mermaid or human, she was so wishy-washy! She would pick one option but then rethink the decision and pick the other option and repeat. Ugh please pick one and stick with it. However, I did LOVE Daniel. He’s definitely my favorite character and there’s more to him than was revealed in this book (at least that’s what I think).<br /><br />I’m probably going to pick up the next book, because I am curious to see what happened.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1371323237921382798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11167311060306055783">Didn't like this one as much as Hocking's Kanin Chronicles, but at least the creepy mermaids twist was interesting. I also liked that it was told from more perspectives, even though a bit messily written. I also ended up likeing Harper and Daniel a million times more than Gemma and Alex neither of whom I gave a shit about since they lacked any kind of personality.   <span id="freeText11167311060306055783" style="display:none">Didn't like this one as much as Hocking's Kanin Chronicles, but at least the creepy mermaids twist was interesting. I also liked that it was told from more perspectives, even though a bit messily written. I also ended up likeing Harper and Daniel a million times more than Gemma and Alex neither of whom I gave a shit about since they lacked any kind of personality. There was a lot of tropes typical for 2010/2012 paranormal books, but mostly in bearable amount. I didn't hate any of the characters, but didn't love them yet either. The plot was way, way too slow. And I think it's because the author wanted to stretch out the story into more books than maybe there should've been. Only the last few chapters really started being interesting and the ending was pretty good.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231313171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9095493864305838778">Well. I couldn't finish this book. And the fact that I couldnt finish it doesn't mean that there's nothing to look forward to it. So keep in mind that my opinion is based only on the first 139 pages of the advance reader's copy of this book.<br/><br/>I like Amanda Hockings' writing, but this book really didn't do it for me.<br/><br/>I got until page 139 of 309 (from arc) and I am still waiting for the story to take off. Only after 120 pages something finally happened, but the problem was that "that something" wasn'</span>
  <span id="freeText9095493864305838778" style="display:none">Well. I couldn't finish this book. And the fact that I couldnt finish it doesn't mean that there's nothing to look forward to it. So keep in mind that my opinion is based only on the first 139 pages of the advance reader's copy of this book.<br /><br />I like Amanda Hockings' writing, but this book really didn't do it for me.<br /><br />I got until page 139 of 309 (from arc) and I am still waiting for the story to take off. Only after 120 pages something finally happened, but the problem was that "that something" wasn't explained soon enough and I just got bored of waiting (Although I have a vague idea of what could it be... but not really). So, even though something finally happened, I have no idea what it was. Amanda Hocking is clearly keeping everything a mystery, and even though I love mystery, I don't like when nothing is given away. So, instead of getting myself hooked to the story, I get detached and give up. <br /><br />This book is very short, barely 300 pages, and during the first half of it, very little happens.<br /><br />This book may be a great start of a series, but I couldn't get into it due to it extremely slow pace. <br /><br />If you really have the patience to go all the way to the end, you may enjoy what Amanda Hocking is keeping for the second half of the book. <br /><br /> <br /></span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278673190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11792707634559739538">I got an advance copy of Wake on Wednesday, and I read it in a day. I just love the way <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking' title='Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amanda Hocking</a> builds her characters. She has a way of making you care about each of them. she doesn't write 2 dimensional characters. Even the ones who barely make an appearance in the story, you feel like you know them. And she has a way of writing budding romances that makes me hold my breath and really root for that first kiss. <br/><br/>The only downside to getting the book before the August release date... how mu</span>
  <span id="freeText11792707634559739538" style="display:none">I got an advance copy of Wake on Wednesday, and I read it in a day. I just love the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking" title="Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Hocking</a> builds her characters. She has a way of making you care about each of them. she doesn't write 2 dimensional characters. Even the ones who barely make an appearance in the story, you feel like you know them. And she has a way of writing budding romances that makes me hold my breath and really root for that first kiss. <br /><br />The only downside to getting the book before the August release date... how much longer I'll have to wait to read Lullaby. <br /><br />Definitely recommend picking this one up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11792707634559739538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_800700900" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800700900" />
    <a title="Eilonwy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy"><img alt="Eilonwy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506803497p2/17237503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/800700900?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eilonwy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eilonwy" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy">Eilonwy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250008121" href="/book/show/15826107-wake">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer800700900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2816732913425779716"><blockquote>Sisters Gemma and Harper are having an all-right summer vacation: Gemma, a champion swimmer, is doing great times and has caught the eye of Alex, the cute boy next door, while Harper is getting ready to start college and is flattered by attention from Daniel, a grungy guy who lives on a houseboat. But Gemma has also gained the interest of a group of mysterious, beautiful girls spending the summer in their tourist town ... and that interest may be dangerous to everyone she cares about. </blockquote>I read thi</span>
  <span id="freeText2816732913425779716" style="display:none"><blockquote>Sisters Gemma and Harper are having an all-right summer vacation: Gemma, a champion swimmer, is doing great times and has caught the eye of Alex, the cute boy next door, while Harper is getting ready to start college and is flattered by attention from Daniel, a grungy guy who lives on a houseboat. But Gemma has also gained the interest of a group of mysterious, beautiful girls spending the summer in their tourist town ... and that interest may be dangerous to everyone she cares about. </blockquote>I read this book because about 18 months or so ago, Amanda Hocking got a huge amount of buzz -- she'd sold over a million self-published e-books, and St. Martin's Press gave her a 7-figure contract. So far as I know, this is the first of her direct-to-paper books, for want of a better term. When I first heard of her, I looked up her reviews on Amazon and was startled to see people saying, "This book was good for 99 cents," because I'd never thought of price as being a factor in my judgement of a book. I am often glad I did not pay for a book -- but the fact that I read it for free from my library will not have raised my opinion of it! So I was very curious to see what her books are like. <br /> <br />Well ... this one isn't terrible. But it isn't very good, either. For one thing, there is a Prologue which pretty much gave away the entire story -- so between that and the overly generous details on the jacket flap, there wasn't much suspense for me. The writing is all right -- it doesn't sparkle, but it's perfectly acceptable. The style could use some help, though -- it's seriously tell, tell, tell, and very little show. Sometimes I thought I was reading an outline for the events rather than a story! There's too much awkward backstory shoved into the wrong places. And the dialogue is really spotty. In far too many instances, the characters will have a long, banal conversation -- and then the author will back off and TELL the reader how the conversation went on to what was actually important, and provide a summary of it rather than taking the characters through that discussion! This is downright jarring in a couple places. In addition, despite Hocking's best efforts to tell the reader how the characters are feeling and what they're experiencing, I just never really connected with any of them. This book was much more like watching the characters than like living a story with them. The narrative switches between Gemma's and Harper's POV's, which also got a little repetitive and distracting, rather than bringing any brighter illumination to the plot elements. <br /> <br />The story is fairly interesting and brings up some really compelling questions, which I suppose will be answered in the next two books. But the story-telling just wasn't strong enough for me to care. The only reason I finished this book was so I could say I've read an Amanda Hocking book all the way through. Otherwise, I would have quit at about the halfway mark. <br /> <br />So, not really recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2816732913425779716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_352198600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/352198600" />
    <a title="Nicole " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6847614-nicole"><img alt="Nicole " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426728381p2/6847614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/352198600?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole " href="/user/show/6847614-nicole">Nicole </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6847614-nicole?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6847614-nicole?shelf=bea12">bea12</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6847614-nicole?shelf=summer-2012">summer-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6847614-nicole?shelf=to-trade">to-trade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352198600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11137030418891328394">I read this book in about a day, while (ironically) in my pool. I've noticed a recent increase in mermaid books, but what I loved about Wake was that it wasn't necessarily about mermaids, but rather about sirens, which a lot of the books seem to be more about. This book doesn't even disguise how awful the sirens are either.<br/><br/>What I love most about taking a pre-existing myth or idea is that there are so many ways to twist it into your own. The sirens in Wake are different from the mermaids in Lies </span>
  <span id="freeText11137030418891328394" style="display:none">I read this book in about a day, while (ironically) in my pool. I've noticed a recent increase in mermaid books, but what I loved about Wake was that it wasn't necessarily about mermaids, but rather about sirens, which a lot of the books seem to be more about. This book doesn't even disguise how awful the sirens are either.<br /><br />What I love most about taking a pre-existing myth or idea is that there are so many ways to twist it into your own. The sirens in Wake are different from the mermaids in Lies Beneath or the sirens in Fathomless. There are so many different twists. In this particular case, these sirens are just pretty, and mean, brutal killers. What we did learn about Penn, Lexie, and Thea isn't much but its enough to know that they aren't good news. Very clearly they were psycho from the way that they seemed to stalk Gemma as they decided that they wanted her.<br /><br />I felt bad for Gemma as she struggled with trying to be as normal as she could while also trying to navigate what she was. I really liked that Hocking gave us a look at what Gemma's life was like before her change. We came to know what her life was like and how her relationships were such as with her older sister Harper. I felt bad as her relationships suffered because of what happened to her.<br /><br />Wake did a lot of things right in this book, and I really can't wait to see what is going to happen in the next book, due out in November.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11137030418891328394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('390TUQ6zNIMbo4orBRjygp5agrMWXJlP8/S8KJmAuSEDdVaUnZR1HoS0JDK+oavOI5oVMlLfLDGFz623Zv9wjA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uoHDyf9qmw3BNNLLVLji2AE9a2/S+oodiE+5jKq5ncBmKYYMbE3akF4jfNLvAbuUvP387pZ5P2P+dKgTVcZUbQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer1551106879808024926">AMANDA HOCKING is the author of over twenty young adult novels, including the New York Times bestselling Trylle Trilogy and Kanin Chronicles. Her love of pop culture and all things paranormal influence her writing. She spends her time in Minnesota, taking care of her menagerie of pets and working on her next book.<br/><br/>Several of her books have made the New York Times Bestsellers list. Her zombie series</span>
  <span id="freeText1551106879808024926" style="display:none">AMANDA HOCKING is the author of over twenty young adult novels, including the New York Times bestselling Trylle Trilogy and Kanin Chronicles. Her love of pop culture and all things paranormal influence her writing. She spends her time in Minnesota, taking care of her menagerie of pets and working on her next book.<br /><br />Several of her books have made the New York Times Bestsellers list. Her zombie series, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/hollowland-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hollows</a>, has been adapted into a graphic novel by Dynamite. She has published over twenty novels, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/48928-trylle&gt; the Trylle Trilogy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kanin Chronicles</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/watersong-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">the Watersong quartet</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/my-blood-approves-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blood Approves series</a>, the Valkyrie duology<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/150484-valkyrie" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25184362-freeks#other_reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Freeks</em>
</a>.<br /><br />Her next books are the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47590299-the-lost-city" rel="nofollow noopener"> Omte Origins</a>, a trilogy set in the world of the Trylle and Kanin. The first book <em> The Lost City</em> will be out July 7, 2020, and the second book <em> The Morning Flower </em> will be out August 5, 2020. <br /><br />For more info about her and her books, here are some other places to check out and ways to contact her:<br /><br />Website: <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.hockingbooks.com</a><br /><br />Amazon Author Page: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Amanda-Hocking/e/B003H4L762" rel="nofollow noopener">amazon.com/author/amandahocking</a><br /><br />Instagram: <a href="https://instagram.com/amanda_hocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram.com/amanda_hocking/</a><br /><br />YouTube: <a href="https://www.youtube.com/aehocking" rel="nofollow noopener">www.youtube.com/aehocking</a><br /><br /><br />Pinterest: <a href="http://www.pinterest.com/aehocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.pinterest.com/aehocking/</a><br /></span>
